    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_420472058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420472058" />
    <a title="Saru (Queen of Bookland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8496075-saru-queen-of-bookland"><img alt="Saru (Queen of Bookland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539544265p2/8496075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420472058?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saru (Queen of Bookland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saru (Queen of Bookland)" href="/user/show/8496075-saru-queen-of-bookland">Saru (Queen of Bookland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781416995968" href="/book/show/12712060-twice-upon-a-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8496075-saru-queen-of-bookland?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420472058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12821557873441231056"><b>WHAT?????? Just... Just WHAT????!!!!!</b><br/><br/><b>Initial reaction after finishing this book:</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392155ra/755016.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Did Jack just...? And did Phillip...? And is May...? And Lian is...?<br/><br/><b>I NEED THE LAST BOOK NOW.</b> <br/><br/>You have to be kidding me I-I-I just, I...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392155ra/755017.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I am going crazy right now!!!!!!! <br/><br/>fAUKD,v.kfhbvk.fjb.kvl.s <br/><br/>James Riley just totally leaves the reader to wonder what's going to happen next. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Will May end up with Jack? Will Phillip end up with Penelope or will he die? Will Jack and his SISTER (Still trying to process </span></span>
  <span id="freeText12821557873441231056" style="display:none"><b>WHAT?????? Just... Just WHAT????!!!!!</b><br><br><b>Initial reaction after finishing this book:</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392155ra/755016.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Did Jack just...? And did Phillip...? And is May...? And Lian is...?<br><br><b>I NEED THE LAST BOOK NOW.</b> <br><br>You have to be kidding me I-I-I just, I...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392155ra/755017.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I am going crazy right now!!!!!!! <br><br>fAUKD,v.kfhbvk.fjb.kvl.s <br><br>James Riley just totally leaves the reader to wonder what's going to happen next. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Will May end up with Jack? Will Phillip end up with Penelope or will he die? Will Jack and his SISTER (Still trying to process that), be able to overthrow the Wicked Queen. And what about that crow? OH CRAP! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This book is a continuation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7327326.Half_Upon_a_Time" title="Half Upon a Time by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Upon a Time</a> and a GREAT one at that. So let's get more in depth with that. With the good and bad (Yes there are some) aspects of this book.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>The Good</u>
</b><br><br><b>1. The plot</b><br><br>In this book, Jack, May, and Phillip continue on there quest to the Fairy Homelands to find out May's true identity. But upon reaching, they get a HUGE surprise. The Wicked Queen has gotten a Fairy Queen to place the Fairy Homelands under a spell, that causes all that pass through the gate to fall into a sleeping spell. There, they encounter Lian, an eye for the queen. She is fast and is a practically unbeatable opponent for Jack. She informs them that at sunset tomorrow, the Wicked Queen's dragons will arrive to burn the homelands to the ground. Afterwards, they basically try to transport themselves back to The Piper's home, because the Piper is the one who got them to the Homelands in the first place, but they find that he is gone, and in his place are some of the Wicked Queen's allies, including the Wolf King, who honestly scares the crap out of me. So Jack, May, and Phillip run into the Piper's cave, where several kids have gone into but none have come out. Then they find a door at the end of the tunnel, which is opened by a morbidly obese adult dressed in a child's clothing. He welcome them to the Land of Never, (A spoof of Peter Pan's Neverland) Where none of the children ever grow up, and there are chocolate waterfalls, piles of money, you name it they got it. This mildly, well actually more than mildly creeps out our main characters who are the only ones who seem to realize that these children have aged. They try to tell the children, erm adults, that they are adults but they don't believe them. They then rescue King Pan from "pirates" and hoo ha yippy ka yay, a bunch of stuff happens and then they are on the sea with pirates who can help Jack, May, and Phillip find the Sea Witch, who can get rid of the spell on the Fairy Homelands so that May can find out who she is. The captain of the pirates, captain Bluebeard also needs something under the sea, which is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his long lost love, Meghan. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is the basic premise of the story. But there is many plot twists along the way. What I'm basically trying to say is that there was never a dull moment in this book, which I LOVE.<br><br><b>2. The characters</b><br><br>Need I say more? I LOVE Jack. I just want to strangle him in a giant hug!!!!! And Phillip too!!!! May is spunky, which I appreciate. She's not all like "I can't fight sharks that walk on land! I'll just sit here in the corner and wait for Prince Charming to swoop in and save me!" Basically, all of the characters are very well-developed. And I love them all.<br> Me thinking about Jack and Phillip:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365763ra/717923.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Bad</u>
</b><br><br>Well, there's only one thing I didn't like about this book. And it's just an eensy weensy thing, really. I read the first book a while ago, so details about the main plot weren't fresh in my head. The book didn't do such a great job recapping the last book. Which I would've liked. Also, one of the things wasn't quite clear. Who put the Fairy Homelands under a spell? Malevolent the fairy queen turned bad, or who???? <br><br>But basically this was an unimaginably great book. And oh yeah, another thing I loved: All the revelations: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Phillip is Sleeping Beauty's true love! May is Cinderella! Jack has a sister who is Lian! And Lian is actually against the Queen! And May and Jack's romantic tension!*Girlish squeal* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12821557873441231056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_277247870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277247870" />
    <a title="Valerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1879727-valerie"><img alt="Valerie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257225221p2/1879727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277247870?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/1879727-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781416995968" href="/book/show/12712060-twice-upon-a-time">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Percy Jackson fans who are into fairy tales</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277247870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7339380639404779432">Should I be embarassed that I read books like this for fun even though I'm technically an adult? Probably, but since this is the internet I'm not that worried. Everyone who knows me in real life on this site already knows I'm a huge dork who can't seem to grow up properly.<br/><br/>So, I as I mentioned above if you like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15872.Rick_Riordan' title='Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rick Riordan</a>'s stuff I really think you should give this a try. He kind of has that silly satire that I love. If you are the kind of reader that can't take slow paced stories, than this is</span>
  <span id="freeText7339380639404779432" style="display:none">Should I be embarassed that I read books like this for fun even though I'm technically an adult? Probably, but since this is the internet I'm not that worried. Everyone who knows me in real life on this site already knows I'm a huge dork who can't seem to grow up properly.<br /><br />So, I as I mentioned above if you like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15872.Rick_Riordan" title="Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Rick Riordan</a>'s stuff I really think you should give this a try. He kind of has that silly satire that I love. If you are the kind of reader that can't take slow paced stories, than this is definitely the book for you. <i>I</i> was feeling exhausted for these characters about half-way through the book because there is <b>never</b> a break. Wait, there is maybe one near the beginning, I lied. Poor Jack, because to be honest how many times can a person get beat up and still be moving? It takes push-yourself-up-and-try-again to a whole new level. You know when the Hulk (in the Avengers) just grabs Loki like a rag doll and flings him back and forth? It’s like that, just done maybe five more times. The body can only take so much, but I assume since Jack is an Eye he can take a few more hits?<br /> <br />Twice Upon a Time takes place about three months after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7327326.Half_Upon_a_Time__Half_Upon_a_Time___1_" title="Half Upon a Time (Half Upon a Time, #1) by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Upon a Time</a> finishes. The first should be read before this one. May, Phillip, and Jack are all still together trying to find out who May’s parents are but low and behold it’s not that easy to just walk into fairy land and just ask. Some way or another they end up meeting King Pan (or Peter Pan), a bluebeard pirate, King of the World, and a mermaid princess with a past.<br /><br />I might have given the book 5 stars if it wasn’t for May. I thought I’d warm up to her by now and I have but I still find her a bit exasperating. May is no longer sarcastic, but she does a lot of threatening which got tiring because she hardly ever follows through. It's not that I think she should kick everyone’s butt, but it seems like she is more bark than bite. <br /><br />The ending I loved but I’ll keep the details to myself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7339380639404779432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3290404767" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3290404767" />
    <a title="Shelby Adcock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/108651953-shelby-adcock"><img alt="Shelby Adcock" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3290404767?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby Adcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby Adcock" href="/user/show/108651953-shelby-adcock">Shelby Adcock</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3290404767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9264862429575043629">This book is a fantasy/sci-fi novel that would be good for children in grades 3 or 4. This book is about a girl named May and her two friends Jack and Phillip who set out on a search for May's true identity. This cannot be done unless they have help from a "fairy godmother" which seems to be hard for them to find. As they soon start out on their journey, they soon start to realize that the lands that house the fairy godmothers has been shut down from a curse. This is devastating news to the thre</span>
  <span id="freeText9264862429575043629" style="display:none">This book is a fantasy/sci-fi novel that would be good for children in grades 3 or 4. This book is about a girl named May and her two friends Jack and Phillip who set out on a search for May's true identity. This cannot be done unless they have help from a "fairy godmother" which seems to be hard for them to find. As they soon start out on their journey, they soon start to realize that the lands that house the fairy godmothers has been shut down from a curse. This is devastating news to the three friends, but they are determined that they are going to be able to reach these spirits. As the book goes on, the three friends show true determination throughout the story and jump through a lot of obstacles to reach this ability to find her true identity. This was a WOW book for me simply because of how interesting it was to read it! I have never been a fan of sci-fi for fantasy novels since I was a kid, so being intrigued and motivated to finish reading this book was what made it a WOW book for me. <br /><br />Thinking about how I am going to use this in a classroom, there can be so many literacy pathways I can go with this. After we read this book through a combination of literacy circles and read alouds, I can ask students to write their own story in their own perspective if they were one of the three friends. When designing this project, I could also incorporate the current writing standards that we were to address at the time. Aside from lessons that were standards based, I could use this book as a topic for a morning meeting or circle time. After reading the book for the writing lesson, it could easily be used for a topic of discussion among students and the teachers. We could go around in a circle and ask students what they think their secret identity would be or what type of fairy they would want to be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9264862429575043629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9411489-reading-is-my-escape?shelf=sunshine-state-14-15">sunshine-state-14-15</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9411489-reading-is-my-escape?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9411489-reading-is-my-escape?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068583866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8809217197997252178">"Once upon a time, Jack knew better than to do certain things. You didn't waste time trying to find the perfect temperature of porridge in a bear's house. You didn't point out to your extremely furry grandmother how big her fangs were. And you definitely didn't walk through a creepy fog while music from magical pipes drifted in eerily."<br/> <br/>That is the opening paragraph in this second book of the Half Upon a Time series. Jack, May & Phillip are back. In book one, they released the Evil Queen from he</span>
  <span id="freeText8809217197997252178" style="display:none">"Once upon a time, Jack knew better than to do certain things. You didn't waste time trying to find the perfect temperature of porridge in a bear's house. You didn't point out to your extremely furry grandmother how big her fangs were. And you definitely didn't walk through a creepy fog while music from magical pipes drifted in eerily."<br /> <br />That is the opening paragraph in this second book of the Half Upon a Time series. Jack, May &amp; Phillip are back. In book one, they released the Evil Queen from her magical prison and found out May isn't who they thought she was. The trio is now trying to fix their mistakes and find out the truth about May's identity.<br /> <br />This book touches so many different fairy tale stories that I don't know if I can remember them all: the Pied Piper, Peter Pan (here King Pan in the Land of Never), Bluebeard the pirate, the Little Mermaid, Sleeping Beauty and Cinderella. I may have missed some but I think you should read the book just to be sure. Oh and Jack &amp; Jill.<br /> <br />I enjoyed this story and I'm ready to read book 3 and find out how it all ends. I recommend it to anyone who enjoys fairy tale stories or new takes on fairy tales. A great book for reluctant readers in 4-8 grade.</span>

<div id="review_335425508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/335425508" />
    <a title="Paul Lunger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859124-paul-lunger"><img alt="Paul Lunger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353803965p2/5859124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/335425508?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Lunger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Lunger" href="/user/show/5859124-paul-lunger">Paul Lunger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer335425508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17213835449430918005">What happens when you mix the stories of "Peter Pan" & "The Little Mermaid"? You end up with this entertaining novel by James Riley. This time around Jack, May & Phillip start off in the realm of the Fairy Homelands in their continued quest to determine who May really is. Their adventures take them to the land of Never here we encounter Pan & Captain Bluebeard. From there we go under the sea to the realm of mermaids & mermen in order to find the Sea Witch who can help break the spell in the Fair</span>
  <span id="freeText17213835449430918005" style="display:none">What happens when you mix the stories of "Peter Pan" &amp; "The Little Mermaid"? You end up with this entertaining novel by James Riley. This time around Jack, May &amp; Phillip start off in the realm of the Fairy Homelands in their continued quest to determine who May really is. Their adventures take them to the land of Never here we encounter Pan &amp; Captain Bluebeard. From there we go under the sea to the realm of mermaids &amp; mermen in order to find the Sea Witch who can help break the spell in the Fairy Homelands &amp; can move May closer to finding out who she is. Riley does another very good job in his re-telling of these classic tales &amp; keeps the adventure moving along w/ enough wit &amp; story to have you the reader laughing at every turn. The novel does leave a lot of open ends &amp; provides us more info on Jack &amp; why he's on this quest with May which is nice to know there will be a 3rd novel in this entertaining new series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17213835449430918005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_621990098" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621990098" />
    <a title="Bayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3975015-bayla"><img alt="Bayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375025386p2/3975015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621990098?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bayla" href="/user/show/3975015-bayla">Bayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3975015-bayla?shelf=fairy-tales-retellings-and-the-like">fairy-tales-retellings-and-the-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3975015-bayla?shelf=princesses">princesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3975015-bayla?shelf=marvelous-middle-grade">marvelous-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3975015-bayla?shelf=here-be-dragons">here-be-dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621990098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5505954699534725547">Just as fun as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7327326.Half_Upon_a_Time' title='Half Upon a Time by James Riley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Half Upon a Time</a>. Told back and forth between Jack's POV and May's, <i>Twice Upon a Time</i> is full of chaos and things going wrong - who says that fairy tales end happily ever after? I liked seeing the twists on various fairy tales and myths and how they are intertwined, and appreciated seeing May and Jack (and others) grow as characters - in many ways, this is a coming of age story, and a story about identity. I liked how self aware the characters were about the craziness of what was </span>
  <span id="freeText5505954699534725547" style="display:none">Just as fun as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7327326.Half_Upon_a_Time" title="Half Upon a Time by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Half Upon a Time</a>. Told back and forth between Jack's POV and May's, <i>Twice Upon a Time</i> is full of chaos and things going wrong - who says that fairy tales end happily ever after? I liked seeing the twists on various fairy tales and myths and how they are intertwined, and appreciated seeing May and Jack (and others) grow as characters - in many ways, this is a coming of age story, and a story about identity. I liked how self aware the characters were about the craziness of what was going on, and think kids/tweens/teens will really appreciate it. I would recommend this book for middle grade - YA fairy tale lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5505954699534725547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344376616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16962445782412837425">If you like twisted fairy tales, you will like this book! It's probably upper elementary level, though both I and my high schooler enjoyed it as well. If you don't mind fairy-tale style magic, there is nothing objectionable in it--except for the fact that the story doesn't end in the first book! Nor in the second, and the third isn't out yet!!! We can't wait for the third..... <br/>(Be sure to read the author blurb on the inside back cover. It's as funny as the book is!) <br/><br/>If you haven't read the first</span>
  <span id="freeText16962445782412837425" style="display:none">If you like twisted fairy tales, you will like this book! It's probably upper elementary level, though both I and my high schooler enjoyed it as well. If you don't mind fairy-tale style magic, there is nothing objectionable in it--except for the fact that the story doesn't end in the first book! Nor in the second, and the third isn't out yet!!! We can't wait for the third..... <br />(Be sure to read the author blurb on the inside back cover. It's as funny as the book is!) <br /><br />If you haven't read the first book, do that first. There is a surprise ending in the first, that the second will tell you.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1657027113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12520329579500064986">I found Twice Upon a Time to be a thrilling adventure book to read. Twice Upon a Time is an amazing book filled with mystery and it was enjoyable to read. This is a second book in a serie of three books. After a princess, May, learned a big secret about her grandmother, which was revealed in the first book, Half Upon a Time. She and the other main character, Jack go through the adventure of a lifetime. This book is filled with twists in the world of fairy tales. I would recommend this book to my</span>
  <span id="freeText12520329579500064986" style="display:none">I found Twice Upon a Time to be a thrilling adventure book to read. Twice Upon a Time is an amazing book filled with mystery and it was enjoyable to read. This is a second book in a serie of three books. After a princess, May, learned a big secret about her grandmother, which was revealed in the first book, Half Upon a Time. She and the other main character, Jack go through the adventure of a lifetime. This book is filled with twists in the world of fairy tales. I would recommend this book to my classmates because it was a funny, page turner. Since this book is a series, I would want to finish the third book and find out what happens next in the last book. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13387799587443720556">Twice Upon a Time<br/>This book starts back at Jacks grandpa’s place and he is refusing to go on another mission. But they want him to go so he somehow gets roped into the next mission with May and Philip. Now they have to save the Fairy Homelands. But how to get there?   <span id="freeText13387799587443720556" style="display:none">Twice Upon a Time<br />This book starts back at Jacks grandpa’s place and he is refusing to go on another mission. But they want him to go so he somehow gets roped into the next mission with May and Philip. Now they have to save the Fairy Homelands. But how to get there? They find a Piper who can help them get there but when the comeback they find themselves in a weird world They find a pirate but will he help them? And will they be able to save the Fairy Homelands in time. <br /><br />Jack and May to of the main characters in the book are so different.Jack is just a poor boy who somehow gets roped into a mission he wasn’t supposed to be in. While May is a princess and she was meant to be in this mission. Also Jack is so clumsy. Every Time he falls, (which he does a lot) he doesn’t land gracefully while May lands unnaturally perfect. Although they have many differences they both don’t know much about their past. They are different and the same in many ways.<br /><br />This book was an amazing. There were always a lot of things happening and you are never bored. There was tons of action. And there were lots of different settings that changed it up a bit. It kept me sucked in and excited. It had lots of strange and awesome things always happening. It didn’t have a very slow start like some books do. There were lots of twists and turns that kept you anxious. It was super awesome book and I loved it so much. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3130822840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3130822840" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75031596-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515616594p2/75031596.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3130822840?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/75031596-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3130822840&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3130822840" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9177311076508647224">This is the third time I've read this book, and I still enjoyed it.<br/><br/><br/>CONS OF TWICE UPON A TIME<br/><br/>I can't think of any.<br/><br/><br/>PROS OF TWICE UPON A TIME<br/><br/>There was no cursing in this book, first off.<br/><br/>The way the <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[romance <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was dealt with in this book was way less blatant than in book 1, and pulled off way better.<br/><br/>The BANTER! (so much sass)<br/><br/>The plot line was well done.<br/><br/>As always, I loved James Riley's dedication and bio.<br/><br/><br/>OVERALL<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book, and I can't wait to read book 3.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x2kWKFP9eJXC7wi3N5l4baEzkKOOTN7hDpnMRlsX/ZHdBvClzrrTPJwJubavl7G2WOU/jLT7VYk+5IA+uUeBQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IMAIEoER0aLoFnOFcShn0iVzYPsy/XDkjmendfviqYE6r+6fHFZ6C7bwwoTpJq4J3KXP1AhK+4y+GusNGbLVUA==')})
  }
